    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer2087949849300325727">Adrian Mole, now age thirty-four and three quarters, needs proof that Saddam Hussein had weapons of mass destruction so he can get a refund from a travel agency of the deposit he paid on a trip to Cyprus. Naturally, he writes to Tony Blair for some evidence.<br/> <br/>He’s engaged to Marigold, but obsessed with her voluptuous sister. And he is so deeply in debt to banks and credit c</span>
  <span id="freeText2087949849300325727" style="display:none">Adrian Mole, now age thirty-four and three quarters, needs proof that Saddam Hussein had weapons of mass destruction so he can get a refund from a travel agency of the deposit he paid on a trip to Cyprus. Naturally, he writes to Tony Blair for some evidence.<br /> <br />He’s engaged to Marigold, but obsessed with her voluptuous sister. And he is so deeply in debt to banks and credit card companies that it would take more than twice his monthly salary to ever repay them. He needs a guest speaker for his creative writing group’s dinner in Leicestershire and wonders if the prime minister’s wife is available.<br /> <br />In short, Adrian is back in true form, unable—like so many people we know, but of course, not us—to admit that the world does not revolve around him. But recognizing the universal core of Adrian’s dilemmas is what makes them so agonizingly funny.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2087949849300325727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_704262567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/704262567" />
    <a title="Bionic Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19300421-bionic-jean"><img alt="Bionic Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586709362p2/19300421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/704262567?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bionic Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bionic Jean" href="/user/show/19300421-bionic-jean">Bionic Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781405610285" href="/book/show/18376455-adrian-mole-and-the-weapons-of-mass-destruction">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=read-authors-q-t">read-authors-q-t</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer704262567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8671767983035470285">This is the eighth book about Adrian Mole (don't ask ...) who started his literary life in 1982, at the age of thirteen and three quarters. The series of books has kept pace with his age and it feels as though it is winding down. The running joke about the inept Adrian is wearing a bit thin, and to put him in the idiotic situation of writing letters to the prime minister so that he can get a refund on his upcoming foreign holiday, seems too ludicrously contrived to be funny. <br/><br/>The book was written</span>
  <span id="freeText8671767983035470285" style="display:none">This is the eighth book about Adrian Mole (don't ask ...) who started his literary life in 1982, at the age of thirteen and three quarters. The series of books has kept pace with his age and it feels as though it is winding down. The running joke about the inept Adrian is wearing a bit thin, and to put him in the idiotic situation of writing letters to the prime minister so that he can get a refund on his upcoming foreign holiday, seems too ludicrously contrived to be funny. <br /><br />The book was written at the time when Tony Blair warned that Saddam Hussein’s weapons of mass destruction could target the island of Cyprus in 45 minutes. Perhaps you had to "be there". At this distance in time it all seems tiresome and irrelevant. Perhaps it is the sort of flash in the pan book which is wryly amusing just for a few months, and then would disappear without trace - unless it is part of a series. <br /><br />I do not read books about party politics, nor reviews of them, nor usually comment. But this has made me wonder if there are many such humorous books about Brexit, and what chance there is that any future readers will read them - or even talk about the event - in fifteen years' time. Kind of puts it all in perspective.<br /><br />I read very little of the book, so hesitate to rate it. However, one star is my default for abandoned books. It would very probably come out at less than one star if I forced myself to plough through the thing, so one star is what I must put. Two stars on Goodreads is an "OK" rating, but there is no way in which this would be OK reading for me. Apologies to those who get their humour from party politics, or depictions of feebly plodding, very English, middle-aged, middle-class men and the women who surround and bemuse them, or those who just love the series. Please do not let my boredom put you off. <br /><br />The series started on a high note, but for me it has now fizzled out. I have just one more book about Adrian Mole, but my hopes are not high.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8671767983035470285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1807008405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1807008405" />
    <a title="Iona  Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5485612-iona-stewart"><img alt="Iona  Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311366951p2/5485612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1807008405?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iona  Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iona  Stewart" href="/user/show/5485612-iona-stewart">Iona  Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1807008405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4319926089832146767">This is yet another laugh-out-loud Adrian Mole diary. This time he begins the diary at the age of 34, but he is still the same earnest, pedantic, letter-writing Adrian.<br/><br/>He has moved away from his flaky parents’ home into a pricey loft apartment on Rat Wharf, not realizing that there’s a reason for the “rat” appellation. It could also have been called “Aggressive Swan Wharf” for that matter, but we’ll get back to that later.<br/><br/>Adrian is a great admirer of Tony Blair and a staunch believer in the exis</span>
  <span id="freeText4319926089832146767" style="display:none">This is yet another laugh-out-loud Adrian Mole diary. This time he begins the diary at the age of 34, but he is still the same earnest, pedantic, letter-writing Adrian.<br /><br />He has moved away from his flaky parents’ home into a pricey loft apartment on Rat Wharf, not realizing that there’s a reason for the “rat” appellation. It could also have been called “Aggressive Swan Wharf” for that matter, but we’ll get back to that later.<br /><br />Adrian is a great admirer of Tony Blair and a staunch believer in the existence of Saddam’s weapons of mass destruction, and is thus a supporter of Britain going to war.<br /><br />He is a would-be published writer but hasn’t as yet achieved any success in that field; he is working on a book to be entitled “Celebrity and madness” but neither has he yet persuaded any celebrity to allow him to interview him or her on that subject, not surprisingly, considering the title.<br /><br />Adrian is the arranger of a creative writing group that meets regularly though he does not wholly appreciate the literary efforts of the others. One of the members is the elderly Gladys, who keeps writing soppy poems about cats, such as:<br /><br />“Poor Blackie’s up in Heaven,<br />God took her life away,<br />He said, you’ll go to Devon,<br />And have a holiday.”<br /><br />Unfortunately, he has little success in persuading celebrities to visit the group and give a talk; as far as I recall, Cherie Blair doesn't even deign to reply to his letter. Thus, the group rapidly dwindles to only two.<br /><br />Adrian has two sons, Glenn, 17, who is in basic training in the army, and in danger of being sent off to war in Iraq, and a younger son, William, who now lives with his mother in Nigeria.<br /><br />Glenn writes frequent letters to Adrian, but unlike his verbally proficient father, Glenn is sadly lacking in basic grammar and spelling skills. <br /><br />Adrian is still madly in love with his childhood sweetheart, Pandora, who is now a junior minister and a household name. He somehow becomes involved with a woman called Marigold and then with her sister, Daisy, even though Marigold is insisting that he marry her. There are numerous complications.<br /><br />He furnishes his loft apartment with stylish new furniture not to mention curtains for his glass lavatory, whose see-through walls are extremely irritating for the prudish Adrian; but he does so through the kind services of MasterCard and Barclaycard who insist on forcing him to accept thousands of pounds in credit and sending him blank cheques; this, of course, leads to poor Adrian getting into a pretty pickle as far as his finances are concerned.<br /><br />It now only remains to mention the aggressive swans that inhabit the canal adjacent to Adrian’s abode. The leader of the pack, Gielgud, is “particularly vicious” and takes an instant dislike to Adrian. The town council member to whom Adrian complains fails to understand the problem; they won’t help him get rid of the swans but will grant him help with conflict resolution work with his supposed neighbour, Mr. Swan, whom they understand to be the source of the problem.<br /><br />There are many more complications and convolutions in Adrian’s story, including the problems of his parents who can’t find out which romantic partners they wish to have, and those of his gay, blind friend, Nigel.<br /><br />The book is brilliantly written and uproarious and reminds us of what was going on in Britain and the world in 2002 and 2003. The main theme concerns, of course, Adrian’s obsession with the weapons of mass destruction and the war in Iraq.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4319926089832146767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18293839148492821853">I am deducting one star because the general politics of the book is a strangely British combination of do-nothingism and liberal fetish. But I am still a bit awestruck that Townsend wrote a book of this size with a humour that never, ever got tedious, even with the politics, on a beach in eastern Europe with 30 lesser books cycling through my brain. It's possible I am the most demanding of all when it comes to humour, and I have such an absolutely begrudging, absolutely astonished admiration for</span>
  <span id="freeText18293839148492821853" style="display:none">I am deducting one star because the general politics of the book is a strangely British combination of do-nothingism and liberal fetish. But I am still a bit awestruck that Townsend wrote a book of this size with a humour that never, ever got tedious, even with the politics, on a beach in eastern Europe with 30 lesser books cycling through my brain. It's possible I am the most demanding of all when it comes to humour, and I have such an absolutely begrudging, absolutely astonished admiration for this style of picaresque in diary form, that I am sharing my admiration for your potential pleasure, even if the politics once made me entirely skip this review.</span>

    <a title="Sara Townsend" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3631520-sara-townsend"><img alt="Sara Townsend" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444079945p2/3631520.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280386373?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Townsend" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Townsend" href="/user/show/3631520-sara-townsend">Sara Townsend</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3631520-sara-townsend?shelf=comic-fiction">comic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280386373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer673187565935538107">I feel like I've grown up with Adrian Mole. I've been following his exploits since I was 13 years old, and as a character fixed in time, he's a year or two older than me.<br/><br/>This book chronicles Adrian's life in 2003, age 34, with the backdrop of the war in Iraq. He worries about his 17-year-old son, who has joined the army and has been deployed to Kuwait, he struggles with a debt problem that's spiralling out of control, and still his love life is as disastrous as ever - he's trying to extricate hi</span>
  <span id="freeText673187565935538107" style="display:none">I feel like I've grown up with Adrian Mole. I've been following his exploits since I was 13 years old, and as a character fixed in time, he's a year or two older than me.<br /><br />This book chronicles Adrian's life in 2003, age 34, with the backdrop of the war in Iraq. He worries about his 17-year-old son, who has joined the army and has been deployed to Kuwait, he struggles with a debt problem that's spiralling out of control, and still his love life is as disastrous as ever - he's trying to extricate himself from the clutches of a needy, clingy young woman called Marigold, whilst fancying her free-spirited sexy sister Daisy.<br /><br />Adrian Mole is a comic character, and it's his flaws and foibles that we laugh about. But ultimately his heart is in the right place, and that's why we're fond of him. In a way it's good that as Adrian grows older he growns no wiser, and he retains the ability to make us laugh. And the fact that Adrian's life is always such a disaster is a source of some reassurance - no matter how bad life gets, it's never as bad as Adrian Mole's.</span>
  <a data-text-id="673187565935538107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312032202?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saffron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saffron" href="/user/show/32482472-saffron">Saffron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780718146894" href="/book/show/820572.Adrian_Mole_and_the_Weapons_of_Mass_Destruction">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312032202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9560715485710485943">As a teenager I loved the Adrian Mole books, and even re-reading the original two again recently I found them still a funny read, more for nostalgia than anything I think.<br/><br/>Moving on to Adrian as an adult, I didn't love the Cappuccino Years, but it was okay. This however tested my patience. Adrian as a teenager was amusing as an adult, down right irritating but it was Marigold that killed it for me. I know she is meant to be an emotional vampire that you hate and that it the point of her character</span>
  <span id="freeText9560715485710485943" style="display:none">As a teenager I loved the Adrian Mole books, and even re-reading the original two again recently I found them still a funny read, more for nostalgia than anything I think.<br /><br />Moving on to Adrian as an adult, I didn't love the Cappuccino Years, but it was okay. This however tested my patience. Adrian as a teenager was amusing as an adult, down right irritating but it was Marigold that killed it for me. I know she is meant to be an emotional vampire that you hate and that it the point of her character but knowing so many people like this in my past I just couldn't read any more of it. Adrian is such a pathetic woos too, he was actually getting somewhere in the last book, in this it's just regressing to childhood idiocy.<br /><br />269 pages in and I gave up and won't be following his journey through life any further because frankly Adrian, you are pathetic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9560715485710485943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15428262961226080188" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1555080886i/27354248._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/m00047t0">https://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/m000...</a><br><br>The fifth book in our series of readings from Adrian’s diaries, written by Sue Townsend. It starts in 2002 and covers the controversial period of the Iraq War.<br><br>Adrian is 34, working in a bookshop in Leicester and about to become the proud owner of a trendy loft apartment. His single status is about to change too, putting further strain on his already stretched finances. As war looms, Adrian is unwavering in his support for Prime Minister Tony Blair and military action, even though his eldest son Glenn is facing deployment to the Gulf.<br><br>Sue Townsend was born in Leicester in 1946. She left school at 15 and was a single parent with three young children by the age of 23. Like Adrian, she wrote in secret for many years, and acknowledged that they often shared the same views - Adrian "C’est moi," she once said.<br><br>First published in 1989, Adrian Mole’s diaries were instant bestsellers and Adrian, the remarkably resilient underdog, quickly became a national treasure. While recording the experiences of one individual and showcasing Sue's fearless and razor sharp wit, the diaries also illustrate how socio-political matters of the time affected the lives of ordinary people.<br><br>Copyright Siegfried Sassoon by kind permission of the Estate of George Sassoon<br><br>Reader: Harry McEntire<br>Abridger: Sara Davies<br>Producer: Alexa Moore<br><br>A Pier production for BBC Radio 4</span>

<div id="review_1580200317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1580200317" />
    <a title="Sara Eames" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24633407-sara-eames"><img alt="Sara Eames" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588690079p2/24633407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1580200317?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Eames" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Eames" href="/user/show/24633407-sara-eames">Sara Eames</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1580200317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13875457168634279873">I first read the Adrian Mole diaries when I was at school but soon stopped reading them. However, at my book swap, I noticed this one on the table and thought I would revisit Mole and see how his life had progressed, as it were. Basically, this is an ok book - a standard Adrian Mole story - amusing at times but not laugh-out-loud funny. Adrian has grown-up (sort of) but still takes no responsibility for his life. Some fo the situations he found himself in were frustrating - you just wanted him t</span>
  <span id="freeText13875457168634279873" style="display:none">I first read the Adrian Mole diaries when I was at school but soon stopped reading them. However, at my book swap, I noticed this one on the table and thought I would revisit Mole and see how his life had progressed, as it were. Basically, this is an ok book - a standard Adrian Mole story - amusing at times but not laugh-out-loud funny. Adrian has grown-up (sort of) but still takes no responsibility for his life. Some fo the situations he found himself in were frustrating - you just wanted him to take control of his life and stop being such an idiot. The amount of times he found himself doing something or agreeing to something against his better judgement was annoying. If you knew Adrian Mole in real life, you would probably want to slap him. There are a couple of semi-poignant moments during the book, but, on the whole, this is harmless fluff. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13875457168634279873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1004132473" />
    <a title="Richard Barnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4322945-richard-barnes"><img alt="Richard Barnes" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1004132473?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Barnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Barnes" href="/user/show/4322945-richard-barnes">Richard Barnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141015880" href="/book/show/820569.Adrian_Mole_and_the_Weapons_of_Mass_Destruction">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1004132473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18124227760085759595">Quite simply the finest and funniest and most moving skewering of Blair's era and his grand folly.<br/><br/>The shallowness of early 21st century Britain is exposed as even Mole, surely the most unfashionable man on Earth, gets caught up (living a lifestyle, not a life as one character puts it). His love life goes through one of its most tumultuous periods with one of his most appalling partners (which is saying something).<br/><br/>Townsend's skills hit their height here, where she deftly brings the laughs and the</span>
  <span id="freeText18124227760085759595" style="display:none">Quite simply the finest and funniest and most moving skewering of Blair's era and his grand folly.<br /><br />The shallowness of early 21st century Britain is exposed as even Mole, surely the most unfashionable man on Earth, gets caught up (living a lifestyle, not a life as one character puts it). His love life goes through one of its most tumultuous periods with one of his most appalling partners (which is saying something).<br /><br />Townsend's skills hit their height here, where she deftly brings the laughs and then the tears together. She hated the Tories, but it seems that her reaction to Blair and his war are harsher still - this is precisely what a Labour Government shouldn't be doing, this is an act of appalling betrayal - and Townsend aimed her pen right into the heart of it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18124227760085759595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

She dictated it to her husband. also, she was working on a sixth Adrian Mole novel when she died, entitled Pandora's Box. </span>

This was a good one off light read.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132923-lighthearted?shelf=humorous-fiction">humorous-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113808237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7174371033852478629">Adrian Mole is now 34 3/4 years old and as the story begins he has canceled his holiday in Cyprus because of Tony Blair’s warnings that Saddam Hussein’s weapons of mass destruction could target the island in 45 minutes. Unfortunately, his travel agent won’t refund his deposit until evidence of the WMDs is put forward. Soooo, true to form, Adrian writes a series of letters to Mr. Blair requesting that Mr. Blair provide this proof to said travel agent.<br/><br/>Although the war does bring a sad note to the </span>
  <span id="freeText7174371033852478629" style="display:none">Adrian Mole is now 34 3/4 years old and as the story begins he has canceled his holiday in Cyprus because of Tony Blair’s warnings that Saddam Hussein’s weapons of mass destruction could target the island in 45 minutes. Unfortunately, his travel agent won’t refund his deposit until evidence of the WMDs is put forward. Soooo, true to form, Adrian writes a series of letters to Mr. Blair requesting that Mr. Blair provide this proof to said travel agent.<br /><br />Although the war does bring a sad note to the story (Adrian’s son is called to action), this is still a humorous glimpse into the life of a mostly lovable but clueless character. Despite the fact that he is now in his thirties, Adrian is still touchingly naive and surprisingly gauche. The naivete still works for me but some of his blundering simply isn’t as humorous as it was when he was a teenager. That said, I still enjoyed the book. I love the accounts of Gielgud the Swan and the related correspondence between Adrian and Trixie Meadows of the City Council. I love the relationship between Adrian and his son, Glen. I love the Robbie storyline even though it is heart-wrenching. I was annoyed by the relationship between Adrian and Marigold but c’est la vie.<br /><br />Others’ reviews of Adrian Mole and the Weapons of Mass Destruction have been mixed as well. There is much praise for Sue Townsend’s flair for satire which is warranted. There is some debate over Adrian’s likeableness this time around, but I don’t think there’s any doubt that he comes across as a very real, human character.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17879564999967593051" style="display:none">This particular book felt contrived to shoehorn in as many of the current news items as possible from the time of writing. <br /><br />Adrian continues to be irresponsible, immature, stupid with a capital S, and frankly, bloody annoying! <div id="review_3098892091" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3098892091" />
    <a title="Realini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7873218-realini"><img alt="Realini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420269105p2/7873218.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3098892091?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Realini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Realini" href="/user/show/7873218-realini">Realini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7873218-realini?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3098892091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16603381826003736981">Adrian Mole and the Weapons of Mass Destruction by Sue Townsend<br/>Eight out of 10<br/><br/><br/>Given the tremendous success of The Secret Diary Adrian Mole, Aged 13 ¾ - <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://realini.blogspot.com/2019/12/the-secret-diary-of-adrian-mole-aged-13.html'>http://realini.blogspot.com/2019/12/t...</a> - listed on The Guardian’s 1,000 Novels Everyone Must Read list, it is only natural to expect sequels, although as the case often is, what follows an acclaimed work does not rise to the level of the first installment – for the sixth ‘episode in the series’, one critic is right in observing that the ‘immatu</span>
  <span id="freeText16603381826003736981" style="display:none">Adrian Mole and the Weapons of Mass Destruction by Sue Townsend<br />Eight out of 10<br /><br /><br />Given the tremendous success of The Secret Diary Adrian Mole, Aged 13 ¾ - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://realini.blogspot.com/2019/12/the-secret-diary-of-adrian-mole-aged-13.html">http://realini.blogspot.com/2019/12/t...</a> - listed on The Guardian’s 1,000 Novels Everyone Must Read list, it is only natural to expect sequels, although as the case often is, what follows an acclaimed work does not rise to the level of the first installment – for the sixth ‘episode in the series’, one critic is right in observing that the ‘immature and angst ridden personality has lost its appeal as Mole approaches middle age’.<br /><br />Indeed, in the Mass Destruction book, Adrian Mole is 33 ¾ years old and much less endearing for the usual person, considering that he is a frenetic fan of Tony Blair, who has descended into something much worse than obscurity in the meanwhile, albeit the undersigned has seen him recently in a CNN interview and was flabbergasted at the quality of this now loathed politician, especially when compared with the likes of Trump and Corbyn.<br />One of the main themes, if not the capital, paramount one, is the War in Iraq, which is addressed in the tile and throughout the novel, in the first few chapters the hero is definitely on the side of the alliance against Saddam Hussein – such as this reader, who understands the blunders, false justifications, self-fulfilling prophecies involved in the decision to attack Iraq, but still, as one who has lived under Ceausescu still feels the attempt to depose a tyrant is justified, even if it is next to impossible to predict what happens when he will have been gone and at times, it can seem worse than the dictatorship in the aftermath…<br /><br />Mole seems to be the only one who supports the war, at one time even when his love affair appears to be compromised, nay, annulled by his stand on the ‘vicious war’, for others around him are so frantic on the issue as to declare that he should ‘stop any communication, telephone, fax, anything’ which is what ‘hedonistic’ Daisy Flowers expects of him, given his attachment to a politician that has lied so catastrophically.<br />Another one that has such a perilous, combative stand on the Iraq War is Pandora Braithwaite, the one we are so familiar with from the first and best of all, The Secret Diary of Adrian Mole, where she shared the spotlight with the hero and she was the second most important character, but after that passage, she will have become a Labor MP, but holding a position on the war that is against that of the leader of the party and thus having to face the prospect of a castaway.<br /><br />The confused hero has a challenging relationship with Marigold Flowers, because after the first fulminating rapprochement, the man is less and less interested, while the girl seems ever more determined to place the affair on a permanent path and somewhat manages to ‘consecrate’ their bond, first by declaring a medical emergency and profiting from it by a sort of emotional extortion and then stating that she is carrying the boyfriend’s child and pretending they are engaged.<br />Granted, Mole does not rise to the occasion, on one hand because of his ‘good nature, but on the other, it because he is weak, somewhat undecided, even when he is pressed by the sister of the false fiancée, Daisy, with whom he has started a real love relationship, to a degree also troubled, for though more enticing, Daisy has her own shortcomings, her sincerity is plagued by a nasty way of swearing and being brutal in her openness.<br /><br />Bruce ‘Brainbox’ Henderson may come to the rescue when Adrian is unable to take the bull by the horns, be a man and address the problem with genuine decisiveness and tell the would be wife the truth, as pressed upon him by Daisy, as he would travel to join Marigold on her recuperating holiday in Italy and get close to her there, to the point of becoming her new boyfriend and possibly more than that.<br />Glenn Mole is the son of the hero, existing before this book, presumably born somewhere in one of the previous four novels, and he joins the War effort and is eventually sent to Iraq, from where he shares his experiences with his father, from the tragicomic encounter with the kids, which are offered candies and one of them seems to be on the point of suffocating and that leads to a series of clashes…<br /><br />The first successes in the conflict are followed by a situation in which, as the son puts it, ‘half the population is happy that Saddam is gone and the other half is very aggressive, the problem being they don’t know how to identify who comes close to them and they have to wear helmets all the time and they find it next to impossible to communicate with the locals’<br />Robbie Stainforth is the Glenn’s friend, also fighting in the Iraqi War, a timid man, who may become a casualty of the conflict, who has an emotional, sensitive side, proved by the fact that he enjoys the books sent by Mole and his employer and he would learn by heart one of the poems in a collection, written by those who took part in World War I, albeit he would be too shy to say it over the phone, when asked to.<br /><br />The Weapons of Mass Destruction do not exist, though the undersigned has no problem with that – to try a sick joke on the subject – thinking that it was still a rather sensible decision to try and get rid of a dictator – to repeat the notion: having lived under Ceausescu, one knows that any effort to depose such a tyrant is more than welcome, even if there are always those who would regret the bastard…in our country today, you still find apparatchiks, old fools, damn nomenclature who would insist to the end of time that it was better when people were starving, queuing for bread and anything else – some items were nonexistent, no matter where you went to find them – being jailed for speaking against the idiots in command…just like Trump’s America – kidding again.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16603381826003736981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_494879965" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/494879965" />
    <a title="Victoria Zigler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9194956-victoria-zigler"><img alt="Victoria Zigler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446997452p2/9194956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/494879965?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria Zigler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria Zigler" href="/user/show/9194956-victoria-zigler">Victoria Zigler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer494879965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18004335807898591919">For the most part this was another exceelent addition to this series. However, it was spoiled for me a little by the way a blind character was handled. I appreciate that most people haven't had much contact with visually impaired people, so the main character's initial behaviour towards him is understandable. I have to say though, speaking as a blind person who went through sight loss as an adult myself, if my friends continued to act that way to me - doing things like leading me by the front of</span>
  <span id="freeText18004335807898591919" style="display:none">For the most part this was another exceelent addition to this series. However, it was spoiled for me a little by the way a blind character was handled. I appreciate that most people haven't had much contact with visually impaired people, so the main character's initial behaviour towards him is understandable. I have to say though, speaking as a blind person who went through sight loss as an adult myself, if my friends continued to act that way to me - doing things like leading me by the front of my t-shirt so I hit things all the time, just to use one example - I wouldn't stay their friend. It wouldn't have been so bad if the author had used those experiences as learning experiences for the main character, and shown him improving in his interaction with the blind character. But there was no improvement in the behaviour towards the blind character, or even evidence that the blind character was showing he was more than just a disabled person who needed others to do things for him. Either the main character is even less observant than I thought, or the author should have spoken to a few blind people before writing her blind character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18004335807898591919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer634359751825264021">Oh Adrian what a disappointment you brought on me. And why? <br/>I loved Adrian Mole books as a teenager. I found him witty, a bit ridiculous, original, fresh - he was great. Then I had a long break. I didn't follow through after the first two books. I excitedly grabbed this one from my mom in law's bookcase... and the rest goes only downhill form there.   <span id="freeText634359751825264021" style="display:none">Oh Adrian what a disappointment you brought on me. And why? <br />I loved Adrian Mole books as a teenager. I found him witty, a bit ridiculous, original, fresh - he was great. Then I had a long break. I didn't follow through after the first two books. I excitedly grabbed this one from my mom in law's bookcase... and the rest goes only downhill form there. No amount of nostalgia will make up for a fact that Adrian Mole is just... pitiful and pathetic. <br /><br />Humour is gone, wit is gone. There is still nice English, but that will not do. The book was so far from the reality it was actually painful to read sometimes. I understand there are Peter Pans among both men and women but Adrian Mole in this book is a brand new level of that. <br /><br />For a moment I thought that ok, it is just using too sharp of a picture to ridicule certain traits. But this went way past the moment of showing flaws of English (European?) society in a ridiculed way. Here it got unrealistically real and it just wasn't funny anymore, it was just sad. <br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2975786591?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaun Nightshade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaun Nightshade" href="/user/show/99608319-shaun-nightshade">Shaun Nightshade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781407477848" href="/book/show/37768829-adrian-mole-and-the-weapons-of-mass-destruction">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2975786591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17882893170905478531">Adrian Mole has been around for many years. I read the original story a few years back and now had a great offer on this audio book. I loved the humour and voice of Adrian in the original series and hoped that an older Adrian had lost none of his honesty and adrianess.<br/><br/>I wasn’t disappointed, the narrator did a very good job and came across well as the star. Adrian is still the same loveable (?) character he was before, still having problems with his love life and dare I say profoundly in love wit</span>
  <span id="freeText17882893170905478531" style="display:none">Adrian Mole has been around for many years. I read the original story a few years back and now had a great offer on this audio book. I loved the humour and voice of Adrian in the original series and hoped that an older Adrian had lost none of his honesty and adrianess.<br /><br />I wasn’t disappointed, the narrator did a very good job and came across well as the star. Adrian is still the same loveable (?) character he was before, still having problems with his love life and dare I say profoundly in love with Pandora, who is now a labour MP. In many ways he hasn’t grown up at all. The world seems to have moved on, yet he still has all his teenage angst in tact. Except now he has two sons, each with a different women, neither of whom live with him.<br /><br />Now Adrian, still an aspiring writer works in a book shop and is in the process of buying a modern flat in Rat Wharf. The story is incredibly funny at times, yet behind the laughter is a tragic tale that brings you down to earth in one of those tricky moments where you realise that it’s not nice to be laughing. Rising debts and a failure, like most of us, to take on more debt seem to be an epitaph to the noughties.<br /><br />It’s the first audiobook I’ve listened to in a long while in full and I have to say this was ideal for an hour a day or so relaxing. Even the cat seemed to enjoy the voice and the story, although I think she fell asleep 😉 Overall a brilliant read and well worth the listen, or read 😉</span>
  <a data-text-id="17882893170905478531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6303741109876590984" style="display:none">It's part of Adrian Mole's emotional blindness that, at the turn of the century, he devoutly believes Iraq had weapons of mass destruction.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2330445886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13746582915660362241">The seventh book in Sue Townsend's long-running Adrian Mole series, Weapons of Mass Destruction centers (not unexpectedly) upon the Blair years and Iraq War. Although I have enjoyed all of the Diaries of Adrian Mole, I did find this volume to be a bit of a slog. I stopped and started several times, and it has taken me the best part of the year to bother returning to it. Though I have listened to the earlier books many times and in many adaptations, I doubt that I will listen to this one again. <br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText13746582915660362241" style="display:none">The seventh book in Sue Townsend's long-running Adrian Mole series, Weapons of Mass Destruction centers (not unexpectedly) upon the Blair years and Iraq War. Although I have enjoyed all of the Diaries of Adrian Mole, I did find this volume to be a bit of a slog. I stopped and started several times, and it has taken me the best part of the year to bother returning to it. Though I have listened to the earlier books many times and in many adaptations, I doubt that I will listen to this one again. <br /><br />The narration is well suited to the character, but in many ways it felt very much like it was rehashing old ground, and Mole's growth (as a partner, employee, and father) felt more like a footnote than a genuine revelation. It has not dimmed my appreciation of the earlier books, or the character, however.</span>

  <span id="freeText5618858764852111123" style="display:none">Adrian Mole and the Weapons of Mass Destruction is an enjoyable read that moves the life of Adrian Mole along nicely.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qU0kxZ4PFzkmAO+TBczJ+Unt+zX6FErC5D8ThIc1IIZMBvv9AT9uN7hwa1KRu3x+Jj6KwwPh+Mz04VPeE7EeSQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pbpdfSYeBKtD3xJQxd+SXVxk+Otf+niJ7rM3qa8sf9VA8YJFuS59pd2vlpFRqCfaM7eJHaYPyof+bXfzO6hBGg==')})
  }

Sadly, the show battled against poor scheduling, having been put up against News at Ten, then in its heyday. Due to declining ratings, a single catastrophic hitch (the killing of a guest on air) and the dumbing down of network TV, Alan’s show was cancelled. Not to be dissuaded, he embraced this opportunity to wind up his production company, leave London and fulfil a lifelong ambition to return to his roots in local radio.\n\nNow single, Alan is an intensely private man but he opens up, for the second time, in this candid, entertaining, often deeply emotional – and of course compelling – memoir, written entirely in his own words. <span id="freeTextContainer11278991639294737004"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br/><br/>Susan Lillian "Sue" Townsend is a British novelist, best known as the author of the Adrian Mole series of books. Her writing tends to combine comedy with social commentary, though she has written purely dramatic works as well. She suffered from diabetes for many years, as a </span>
  <span id="freeText11278991639294737004" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br /><br />Susan Lillian "Sue" Townsend is a British novelist, best known as the author of the Adrian Mole series of books. Her writing tends to combine comedy with social commentary, though she has written purely dramatic works as well. She suffered from diabetes for many years, as a result of which she was registered blind in 2001, and has woven this theme into her work.</span>
